        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer880508174" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17015270682630493838">Review also posted at <a href='http://youngadulthollywood.com/books/yah-book-review-2014-ya-contemporary-round-up/#.VG5lIfnF-So' rel='nofollow noopener'>Young Adult Hollywood.</a><br/><br/>I think my life would be a much better place <i>if</i> books could just stay as their enticing, shinny, gorgeous prose. <br/><br/>Josephine Angelini's Starcrossed Trilogy is one of my favorite Young Adult series. It was relatively easy to get lost into that world despite it's flaws. <br/><br/>I was so ready to liked <i>Trial by Fire.</i> I have quite a few reasons why to like it.<br/><br/><b>A.)</b> I'm a huge fan of witches. I love witches, especially anything that got to do with Salem.<br/><br/><b>B.)</b> <u>ALTERNATE U</u></span>
  <span id="freeText17015270682630493838" style="display:none">Review also posted at <a href="http://youngadulthollywood.com/books/yah-book-review-2014-ya-contemporary-round-up/#.VG5lIfnF-So" rel="nofollow noopener">Young Adult Hollywood.</a><br><br>I think my life would be a much better place <i>if</i> books could just stay as their enticing, shinny, gorgeous prose. <br><br>Josephine Angelini's Starcrossed Trilogy is one of my favorite Young Adult series. It was relatively easy to get lost into that world despite it's flaws. <br><br>I was so ready to liked <i>Trial by Fire.</i> I have quite a few reasons why to like it.<br><br><b>A.)</b> I'm a huge fan of witches. I love witches, especially anything that got to do with Salem.<br><br><b>B.)</b> <u>ALTERNATE UNIVERSE.</u> Do I need to say something more? Guess not.<br><br><b>C.)</b> I was pretty much sold with this book since I first saw that gorgeous cover paired with the lovely text.<br><br>Trial by Fire is certainly a step up from Starcrossed Trilogy. Angelini's writing improved immensely. The plot of this book is much intricate and complex as well, <i>but</i> with all of the Physics's senseless facts and explanation and information dumping. I had a difficult time connecting with the book. <br><br>I greatly appreciate that in Salem, women are the people in charge and power. My inner feminism is so proud with that. Sadly, that festive moment ended right there.<br><br>I wasn't impressed by Worldwalker's characters. They are another bunch of flat, dry and static characters. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1411686077ra/11265120.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Lily Proctor isn't a bad character. From clumsy and quirky protagonist, she evolved in a powerful witch that might be in a brink of monstrous capabilities any minute. Aside, from that Lily and I honestly didn't see each other eye to eye. There's no proof of bonding that ever happened. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1411686077ra/11265121.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Rowan, the love interest, the hero. <s> [INSERT SAD EMOJI]</s> <br>All hope was lost. Rowan isn't the most charming, pants dropping character that ever existed. This is the only thing that <i>could have</i> salvaged the story. I need a new pairing to ship. All of my otps are probably dead, not canon or <i>just</i> a crackship, but TADA!, this search is futile and fruitless.<br><br><b>Final verdict: </b>Not a terrible book, just bland and poorly executed.<br><br><b>Edited: September 25, 2014</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1394731684ra/8897529.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>A NEW JOSEPHINE ANGELINI SERIES ABOUT SALEM WITCHES. COUNT ME IN!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1394730253l/18530258.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>That cover is so beautiful. Macmillan can't never do anything wrong.</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

  <i>“There comes a day when every girl loses the stars in her eyes. And then she can see clearly.”</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/><br/>The next time I decide to underestimate Josephine Angelini and forget how deliciously good and painful her books are, I give you all permission to punch me in the face to remind me why I shouldn't.<br/><br/>Stupid book made me fall in love and then left me in pieces 😤 <br/>I'm so mad rn I had to get the rest of the series🤷🏼‍♀️<br/><br/><br/><br/>RTC (probably. maybe. almost certainly)<br/><br/><br/><b>ACTUAL RATINGS 500/5</b></span>

<div id="review_1036960553" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1036960553" />
    <a title="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library"><img alt="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1350750103p2/4551536.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1036960553?book_show_action=true">Aug 26, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library">Maja (The Nocturnal Library)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=just-another-book-crush">just-another-book-crush</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=open-ending">open-ending</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=creepy-love-triangle">creepy-love-triangle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=reviewed-in-2014">reviewed-in-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=arc-2014">arc-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=all-the-right-choices">all-the-right-choices</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1036960553" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1766779846600943622">Although it has a firm connection to our world, <i>Trial by Fire</i> could very well be considered a fantasy novel. The worldbuilding isn’t particularly elaborate, but it serves the story very well, and it will probably expand in the next two installments, although I don’t really feel that there’s too much to add. While simple, Lillian’s world (as opposed to Lily’s world, which is also ours) is perfectly functional and developed just enough to carry the story easily.<br/><br/>Lily is exactly the type of heroine </span>
  <span id="freeText1766779846600943622" style="display:none">Although it has a firm connection to our world, <i>Trial by Fire</i> could very well be considered a fantasy novel. The worldbuilding isn’t particularly elaborate, but it serves the story very well, and it will probably expand in the next two installments, although I don’t really feel that there’s too much to add. While simple, Lillian’s world (as opposed to Lily’s world, which is also ours) is perfectly functional and developed just enough to carry the story easily.<br><br>Lily is exactly the type of heroine that’s easy to admire and even love. Her own world was never kind to her, not only because of her allergies to just about everything, but because of the difficulties she had to endure socially. Her friendship with Tristan was often the only thing holding her together, so when even that was taken from her rather cruelly, the episode was almost too difficult to bear.<br><br>Tristan’s unforgivable actions at the beginning of this story caused me to fear that Lily would somehow end up back in their unequal, dysfunctional dynamic, but she was spared from it both by her crossing into Lillian’s world, and by her own strength which wouldn’t allow her to be anyone’s inferior for long. On the other side, she met Lillian’s Tristan which was once again cause for some concern, but while he shared many similarities with Lily’s, his existence was heavily marked by Rowan’s, who was inexplicably absent from Lily’s world. Tristan’s affection for Lillian/Lily was quite evident, but so was his peace with the fact that he’d always come second to Rowan. The romantic feelings that threatened to develop between them never even so much as sparked as Rowan’s strong presence overtook both the story and the possibility of gaining Lily’s affection.<br><br>I must confess that Lily and Rowan’s relationship of trust and attraction made me a bit uneasy at times. On the surface, it was pure perfection, slowly built from dislike and mistrust to strong friendship and perhaps even something more. But I couldn’t force myself to forget the fact that Rowan was once intimate with a different version of Lily, and that he loved Lillian strongly, even though she wronged him, and every time I thought about it, I found it infinitely creepy.<br><br>Despite my focus on the romance in this review, I should mention that the book’s focus is primarily on Lily herself and her long journey. The path from childish infatuation with Tristan to mature, genuine feelings she developed for Rowan is just one of the things that show her tremendous growth in this book. Wherever she goes and whatever she does next, I’ll be her ally until the very end.<br><br><br><a href="http://www.thenocturnallibrary.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380226536i/681142.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aly (In Wonderland)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aly (In Wonderland)" href="/user/show/22178203-aly-in-wonderland">Aly (In Wonderland)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22178203-aly-in-wonderland?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22178203-aly-in-wonderland?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1037898078" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7699107613640008786"><a href='http://magazine.100percentrock.com/reviews/book-reviews/201502/99109' rel='nofollow noopener'>To read the full review, CLICK ME!</a><br/><br/><i>
  <blockquote>"Funny how quickly the mind moves, but how slowly time does when you're in pain."</blockquote>
</i><br/><br/>Whilst the fantasy and magical elements were incredibly well executed, I found myself confounded by Lily. I couldn't buy into her innocent goody-two-shoes personality and then her quick, immediate switch to badass witch wielding powerful magic like a baton. It was too sudden and very hard to get used to. I wanted Lily to grow into her magic and feel the power before turning into</span>
  <span id="freeText7699107613640008786" style="display:none"><a href="http://magazine.100percentrock.com/reviews/book-reviews/201502/99109" rel="nofollow noopener">To read the full review, CLICK ME!</a><br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>"Funny how quickly the mind moves, but how slowly time does when you're in pain."</blockquote>
</i><br /><br />Whilst the fantasy and magical elements were incredibly well executed, I found myself confounded by Lily. I couldn't buy into her innocent goody-two-shoes personality and then her quick, immediate switch to badass witch wielding powerful magic like a baton. It was too sudden and very hard to get used to. I wanted Lily to grow into her magic and feel the power before turning into a machine. Some of her decisions also made it hard to feel sorry for her, considering they were incredibly stupid and could've been prevented if only she'd had an inch of common sense. It was also difficult to see the romance as romance when, in real Salem, Lily was so head over heels for Tristan. Two days pass in alternate Salem and, suddenly, Lily can't see life without Rowan.<br /><br /><s>

<div id="review_1622214386" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1622214386" />
    <a title="Donita Luz" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18877120-donita-luz"><img alt="Donita Luz" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1447515803p2/18877120.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1622214386?book_show_action=true">Apr 27, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Donita Luz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Donita Luz" href="/user/show/18877120-donita-luz">Donita Luz</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18877120-donita-luz?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18877120-donita-luz?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18877120-donita-luz?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18877120-donita-luz?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18877120-donita-luz?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18877120-donita-luz?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18877120-donita-luz?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18877120-donita-luz?shelf=2016-read">2016-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1622214386" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15259271490225340248"><b>Trial by Fire</b> has the potential to be not just a good read but one of the best urban fantasy read for me given its unique premise and unpredictable plot, if only it has a better execution. <blockquote>
  <i>"Heat builds around me, and the fire begins to eat into my flesh. Yes, fire has teeth, and it chews at you like a living, breathing animal. It even roars like an animal. When you are in its mouth, you have to fight for air. Fire, like a lion, likes to suffocate its prey."</i>
</blockquote> When I started this book, I was ha</span>
  <span id="freeText15259271490225340248" style="display:none"><b>Trial by Fire</b> has the potential to be not just a good read but one of the best urban fantasy read for me given its unique premise and unpredictable plot, if only it has a better execution. <blockquote>
  <i>"Heat builds around me, and the fire begins to eat into my flesh. Yes, fire has teeth, and it chews at you like a living, breathing animal. It even roars like an animal. When you are in its mouth, you have to fight for air. Fire, like a lion, likes to suffocate its prey."</i>
</blockquote> When I started this book, I was having a hard time putting it down. I have a lot of hypothesis on how this story would eventually turn out but none of them happened in this book. Either I'm really bad at thinking of a good plot(which I doubt) or this book is really unpredictable. I'm betting it's the latter. <br><br>Lily, has been sick and in love with her best friend all her life. So when she thought their relationship is actually turning into something more than just friendship, she grabbed it and embraced it, even if it means doing something really stupid and dangerous by going to a party where smoke and alcohol can get into her system and trigger her allergies and can kill her on the spot. If she could just be very careful and Tristan's there, it shouldn't be any problem... Right?<br><br>Of course there was a problem! The night which was supposed to be one of the best night in lily's high school life turned out to be a nightmare. So first chance she get on leaving and disappearing on her world, she took it, without even realizing that escaping her world meaning going to a fantasy or alternate world.<br><br>Now isn't that interesting enough for you to want to read this? Trial by Fire contains alternate fantasy world and witches that burn for <b>power</b>! I mean, isn't it a customary that people burn witches to kill them off? That was one of the few things that I find really interesting in the premise of this book. It has the combination of magic, alternate universe and (i thought would be) interesting and believable romance. <b>However, where the premise and story was really good, it fell short on character and romance development.</b> It's too bad that characters are what usually can make or break a YA book for me. <br><br>Lily, the main character, was supposed to be strong and powerful, however I have never seen her grew strong in the whole duration of the book, and it frustrates me! I mean, I could understand how she came out as weak and sickly on the first part of the book but I was expecting a warrior lady witch in this new fantasy world she was in. Oh but no, because she was busy sorting out her feelings for Tristan in this world, who also is her best friend in her contemporary world and the new boy she hasn't met before, Rowan.<br><br><b>Then there's the romance where I didn't swoon one bit.</b> <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1462710160ra/19033720.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The romance fell flat on me. I don't know if it has something to do with Rowan who never warms up to me. I can't feel anything for him. He seems like a strong and wonderful person sure, but I can't seem to connect with him. If I were Lily, I don't know what to feel about Rowan's affection. I mean, as a reader, I can't even tell if Rowan's feelings for Lily is really for her or was it because she has the same as Lillian's? Good thing there wasn't any love triangle here, and I hope it stays the same for the sequel.<br><br>Anyway, regardless of the issue I encounter reading Trial by Fire, I would still recommend this to people who want to read something new in their YA Urban Fantasy read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15259271490225340248" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer881315189" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16632985865136999020"><b>Initial Impressions 10/2/15:</b> Wow, what an interesting book! I struggled with it at the beginning because "fanta-sci" is hard for me sometimes. It all depends on how it's put together and some fanta-sci flows seamlessly to where I don't even know it's bending and I've read other books where the fantasy and sci-fi elements end up battling each other instead of working together. Once I got into the groove and the feel, I really ended up enjoying it! <br/>I loved how the characters grew throughout the bo</span>
  <span id="freeText16632985865136999020" style="display:none"><b>Initial Impressions 10/2/15:</b> Wow, what an interesting book! I struggled with it at the beginning because "fanta-sci" is hard for me sometimes. It all depends on how it's put together and some fanta-sci flows seamlessly to where I don't even know it's bending and I've read other books where the fantasy and sci-fi elements end up battling each other instead of working together. Once I got into the groove and the feel, I really ended up enjoying it! <br />I loved how the characters grew throughout the book, specifically Lily (of course) since she has the most growing to do. It was interesting to see her strength grow as well as her friendships, familial relationships, and romantic relationships. <br />I didn't quite fall fully in love with it but I did enjoy and appreciate so much of it! I especially enjoyed getting to know Rowan and his backstory and I'm still dying to know more about Lillian and what in the world is up with her. The pieces are starting to fall into place but I can't wait to learn more! I kind of want to just start the next book right away... <br /><br /><b>Full review originally posted <a href="http://www.bookaddictsguide.com/2015/12/02/trial-by-fire-worldwalker-1-josephine-angelini/" rel="nofollow noopener">HERE</a> on The Book Addict's Guide 12/2/15:</b> TRIAL BY FIRE was a really interesting book! I admit that I was a bit hesitant about the mash-up of science-fiction and fantasy with the alternate universe and magical powers merging into one story line but the further I got into the world building, the more I really enjoyed it! It was one of my first adventures into “fanta-sci” (the very first one didn’t go so well) and although it took a bit of adjusting, I really got into Lily’s world in TRIAL BY FIRE!<br /><br />The beginning of the book was a bit slow for me. There were a lot of mixed messages regarding characters in terms of who was good to Lily and who was not so I was on a bit of roller coaster for the first portion of the book trying to get a hold on who I should like and who went on the naughty list… Once all of that sorted itself out and the focus started to turn more to Lily, I rather ended up enjoying things! All of the friendship/relationship drama in her “actual world” (or the world as she knows it) grew a bit tiresome but I also think it was supposed to. Clearly from the synopsis of the book and general concept, the reader knows that Lily is destined for bigger and better things… just in another universe. I was happy and totally hooked to see Lily’s place in the alternate world and what exactly she could do there.<br /><br />The world building and magic system were really interesting for me! It took me a while to really wrap my brain around the fact that we were dealing with an alternate world but then throwing magic in there, but I rather enjoyed that the magic was grounded more in science and that the differences in the world were because of scientific reasons. Once I got to that point, I think I was able to see it more as an alternate universe instead of a fantasy world — even though it was a little bit of both! My brain really just has a hard time merging the two because sci-fi is obviously based on reality, a what-could-have-been, or speculation about the future and a fantasy world is something totally unrelated to our world as we know it. (I supposed there are exceptions to that like urban fantasy, paranormal aspects, and where other mash-ups but since I’m mainly a high fantasy reader, it was a bit harder for me to reconcile).<br /><br />The relationships in the alternate world totally pulled me in too. I loved seeing Lily’s relationship with Rowan develop, as well as how complicated things are for Lily in general given that there’s already a Lily (known as Lillian) in this alternate world. Things really started to get complicated for everyone with a Lily and a Lillian and I got even more curious how Lily was pulled into New Salem to begin with! I loved the growth of each of the characters throughout the book and I was so happy to see Lily really come into her own.<br /><br />TRIAL BY FIRE was definitely enjoyable and by the end of the book, I was sucked into this new fanta-sci world. I wanted to essentially binge read the series but I didn’t end up reading the second book right away so I think I’ll save it for when book three comes out! I’ll need to keep myself up to speed for this exciting series!</span>
  <a data-text-id="16632985865136999020" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17970111484359303276"><b>What a mess of a book.</b><br/><br/>The premise is definitely interesting but I had a lot of problems with the story and the writing. First of all,I'm not a fan of writing from the third-person point of view because I can't completely connect with the characters and that's exactly what happened here - it's not that I just couldn't connect with Lilly and Lillian,it's that I literally didn't care about them. They could've both died and I wouldn't even flinch. Same goes for the supporting characters except for J</span>
  <span id="freeText17970111484359303276" style="display:none"><b>What a mess of a book.</b><br><br>The premise is definitely interesting but I had a lot of problems with the story and the writing. First of all,I'm not a fan of writing from the third-person point of view because I can't completely connect with the characters and that's exactly what happened here - it's not that I just couldn't connect with Lilly and Lillian,it's that I literally didn't care about them. They could've both died and I wouldn't even flinch. Same goes for the supporting characters except for Juliet.The story dragged a lot and it could've been at least 20% shorter. The world Angelini created here is basically a mix of modern and antique mess. I couldn't get used to it and it felt kind of forced. The story is definitely easy to get into but I almost didn't finish it. Rowan is an okay character but I didn't get quite attached to him. The whole process of claiming is weird and confusing,Lillian's actions are supposed to be mysterious but instead they were boring and annoying and Lily/Rowan scenes were too hot and cold for my taste.The only cool thing is that a minor character has the same name as me haha! That awkward moment when I paid the most attention to Gideon's chapters.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1416712098ra/12046760.gif" width="330" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I don't think I'll be continuing with this trilogy anytime soon.</span>

<div id="review_1832404455" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

<span id="freeTextContainer4266565814318668127">Although the magic system was super unique - it being science based and all - I felt like exposition was very much lacking in this first book. It's not often I wish there was more expo, but honestly, I felt so confused about the world that Lily stepped into! I couldn't tell you what time period it was based one, or what the government or economic systems were like, and I have no idea what the characters that aren't magical even do in this world. I kept hoping that things would be explained event</span>
  <span id="freeText4266565814318668127" style="display:none">Although the magic system was super unique - it being science based and all - I felt like exposition was very much lacking in this first book. It's not often I wish there was more expo, but honestly, I felt so confused about the world that Lily stepped into! I couldn't tell you what time period it was based one, or what the government or economic systems were like, and I have no idea what the characters that aren't magical even do in this world. I kept hoping that things would be explained eventually, but no. She's left to explore this new world, with no context as to how it works apart from knowing her other self is some kind of evil tyrant, but not a queen, so...? <br /><br />I was very pleased that there was little to no romance in this first book, but I can only assume that's going to change in the next two. womp womp. <br /><br />Still, I have very high hopes for how this series is going to continue, because all we know really, is that Lily is a crucible, and how that whole gig works. More conflict in book two please! </span>

<div id="review_1032524554" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1032524554" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1032524554?book_show_action=true">Aug 21, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781447260820" href="/book/show/22087268-trial-by-fire">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=magical-fantasy">magical-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2014">read-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1032524554" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11893223329520240022"><b>I literally have only good things to tell you about this book!</b>How's that?! It's absolutely crazy, right?! There's a few things I may or may not whinge about, but they're all so microscopic and variable...pfft. Don't even listen to me. Just drop everything and go read this now. (Unless, of course, you're carrying something precious like a small child or chocolate cake. Then don't drop everything right away.)<br/><br/><b>It's basically a evilly delicious tale about magic, jumping-through-multiple-worlds, scien</b></span>
  <span id="freeText11893223329520240022" style="display:none"><b>I literally have only good things to tell you about this book!</b>How's that?! It's absolutely crazy, right?! There's a few things I may or may not whinge about, but they're all so microscopic and variable...pfft. Don't even listen to me. Just drop everything and go read this now. (Unless, of course, you're carrying something precious like a small child or chocolate cake. Then don't drop everything right away.)<br><br><b>It's basically a evilly delicious tale about magic, jumping-through-multiple-worlds, science, fire, and the occasional pickle. </b> I'm not joking. Pickles feature. Mostly science and magic. I was impressed with the combo of sciencey magic, although (I have to admit) if you even say "biology" in my hearing, my eyes sort of glaze over and I think about pickles and sandwiches. I just don't get science. I do try, occasionally, but to no avail. So that was a bit of a downer for me, but the awesome twist on magic and witches made up for it. The book has it's own rules for magic and they're unique and amazing. I love it when books are original!<br><br>Basically we get thrown into a completely different world. <br><br>It can be challenging to keep up with. The book has a theory that there are millions of versions of our world. Our bonnie main character, Lily, gets tossed into an alternate universe. SO. You'd imagine everything would be different, right? It is. Completely. Which is awesome, but a bit overwhelming and there's lots of explaining.<br><br>You know what I liked about it though? For once, this alternate world DID NOT follow a lot of the average prejudices that most fantasy worlds haul out of our world. They ditch sexism! Hurrah! This world has different values and levels of what's acceptable, honourable, intimate, and edible. That last one is kind of interesting at times. Can I just shout: REFRESHING?!!<br><br><b>The dialogue is epic too! </b> FINALLY. GOOD DIALOGUE. It's funny and deep and realistic. But you know me: laughing is important. Hang on a sec, just awarding the book extra shiny stickers.<br><br><b>So the characters? You want to hear about them right?</b> WELL. First off we have Lily, who is highly allergic to...everything. I totally related to her on that, even though I'm not hyper allergic, I've always had allergies. I'm the person who avoids you if you're wearing hairspray. <br><br>But then Lily bops into the alternate world where another version of her, Lilian, is an evil and very powerful witch. It's soooo much more complicated. Everybody's actions dance in a grey area. So freakishly awesome.<br><br>In the Alternate World, Lily joins up with three incredibly awesome dudes. You think it'd be an insta-love-triangle or something, right? Well, yes, she is sort of attracted to two of the guys, BUT IT'S DIFFERENT. It's somehow not tacky or frustrating or irritating. I absolutely loved Lily, and I adored the three guys (Rowan, Tristan and Caleb). <br><br>The dynamics of the foursome reminded me of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17675462.The_Raven_Boys__The_Raven_Cycle___1_" title="The Raven Boys (The Raven Cycle, #1) by Maggie Stiefvater" rel="nofollow noopener">The Raven Boys</a> by Maggie Stiefvater. Everyone was friends first and then the romances built off that. So awesome. And they were all so well fleshed out and well written! Rowan was totally swoonworthy, but cranky and a little mysterious. (Also a fabulous cook, which I greatly admire.) And Tristan was very smiling and light and winning. Caleb was brute force, good to have around. They just meshed together all so well!<br><br><b>So what are my peeves?</b> They're small, really not worth mentioning, but YOU'RE DYING TO KNOW. I, personally, feel the cover is a bit off. I love it! Don't get me wrong! But I thought it was a romantic contemporary when I first saw it. The USA cover (on the right, below) isn't much better (hey, don't spear me if you like it). It feels too generic and grey. <br> <br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20613491.Trial_by_Fire__Worldwalker___1_" title="Trial by Fire (Worldwalker, #1) by Josephine Angelini" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1396827051s/20613491.jpg" alt="Trial by Fire (Worldwalker, #1) by Josephine Angelini" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>And despite how much I enjoyed reading the book, it felt like it took forever to finish. I was constantly seeing how many pages I had left.</b> I wasn't bored, per se, I was just a centimetre off being totally swallowed. I was distracted. Squirrel. Whatever you want to call it.<br><br><b>Oh and THE ENDING IS AN AWFUL CLIFFHANGER. </b> Awful terrible horrible and mean. (A moaning phrase here, which means: <i>I loved it so much.) </i>Excuse me, I'm just going to collapse sobbing. I need the sequel. I need it quite badly, I will probably even stomp my foot Wicked Witch of the West style because I need the sequel so much.<br><br>There's no reason not to give it 5-stars...except that something makes me hesitate. <b>Therefore 4.5 stars!</b> And I can't wait for the next book! And if you're looking for a fantasy that focus on a) the world building, b) awesome dialogue c) really well fleshed out characters, and d) pickles: THEN THIS IS THE BOOK FOR YOU. <br><br>(I'm kidding, really, about the pickles. It mentions them like<i> once</i>, but they do save lives.)</span>
  <a data-text-id="11893223329520240022" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review1032524554">
  <td colspan="2">

<div id="review_1003087783" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1003087783" />
    <a title="Kassidy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8937622-kassidy"><img alt="Kassidy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585073850p2/8937622.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1003087783?book_show_action=true">Jul 21, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kassidy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kassidy" href="/user/show/8937622-kassidy">Kassidy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8937622-kassidy?shelf=for-review">for-review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8937622-kassidy?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8937622-kassidy?shelf=2014-release">2014-release</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1003087783" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17013945629660272802">*4.5*<br/><br/>One of the things I love most about this book is how intricate this world is. It mixes together magic and science, but yet it almost appears medieval. I also love how in depth the explanations go with how the world works. I found it extremely fascinating and unique. Also very interesting were the parallels to our world. There are some things we have in our world that this world has never heard of, and a lot of our 'science' discoveries are explained through magic in this new Salem.<br/>As someon</span>
  <span id="freeText17013945629660272802" style="display:none">*4.5*<br /><br />One of the things I love most about this book is how intricate this world is. It mixes together magic and science, but yet it almost appears medieval. I also love how in depth the explanations go with how the world works. I found it extremely fascinating and unique. Also very interesting were the parallels to our world. There are some things we have in our world that this world has never heard of, and a lot of our 'science' discoveries are explained through magic in this new Salem.<br />As someone who is extremely interested in science, I found this book to be very intriguing and thought-provoking.<br /> <br />I also enjoyed Lily's character. She's very head-strong and stubborn, but she always sticks to her character. She has her beliefs and never wavers. Sure, she makes some risky decisions, but she is put in many life-threatening situations. I definitely admired a lot of her choices. Even though she is stubborn, she is intelligent and generally thinks things through. She does make mistakes and has faults, but keeping in mind the insane situation she is put in, I think she dealt with it all very well.<br /> <br />I also like how the story is written. It can be confusing because we are thrown into this new world along with Lily, so she isn't much help in explaining things. However, Angelini includes some alternate POVs to help build the world and explain the workings, along with exploring some political drama. I found these very helpful and also entertaining. These different POVs also allow some character development with the characters in this new world. I love how each character has a distinct personality, even the ones who cross over from Lily's home Salem.<br /> <br />The romance was good for me, I like that it didn't take center stage, but it was there. I can imagine that it will definitely cause drama in the next books!<br /> <br />With all of that said, this book was a little overwhelming for me to read at times. There is a lot of information to take in, and some times I had to put it down so I could process everything. I think this also made it drag slightly and I couldn't completely immerse myself in it. Therefore, I could not give it a full five stars.<br /> <br />This book explores an alternate world that is on the brink of war and a girl who has to save it from her other self. <br /> <br />I was fascinated by the odd mix of medieval and modern, magic and science, and loved learning about this world and characters. I can honestly say that I need the next book right now! The ending was the perfect kind of cliff-hanger.<br /> <br />*Thank you to Macmillan for sending me a review copy of this book in return for an honest review. All opinions are my own.*<br /><br />Originally posted at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://travelingthroughpages.booklikes.com/post/947210/trial-by-fire-by-josephine-angelini">http://travelingthroughpages.booklike...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="17013945629660272802" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<span id="freeTextContainer7855143046451982580">I don't know what I was expecting from this book but I was left a little underwhelmed. That might because I went in to this book knowing nothing, confident that I was going to be reading fantasy, but the first 40 pages were contemporary. I was confused and weirded out. I think it would have worked out better if I knew from that start that this book had alternate universe plot.<br/>I didn't like the characters at all in the beginning. Lily was willing to risk her life (I'm not even kidding) just so sh</span>
  <span id="freeText7855143046451982580" style="display:none">I don't know what I was expecting from this book but I was left a little underwhelmed. That might because I went in to this book knowing nothing, confident that I was going to be reading fantasy, but the first 40 pages were contemporary. I was confused and weirded out. I think it would have worked out better if I knew from that start that this book had alternate universe plot.<br />I didn't like the characters at all in the beginning. Lily was willing to risk her life (I'm not even kidding) just so she could go to a party with a boy. A boy who was her friend for years but molested her in her sleep one night(but Lily was totally okay with that). Within 20 pages Lily wised up and told the boy to leave, which was great, but her change of heart was very sudden and out of place. Everything happened really fast and was so rushed. <br />I liked the plot though. I thought it was really cool and different. Not always well executed but it had it good points. <br />Overall, Trial by Fire was pretty good. It had highs and lows but it was pretty good. It's not the best fantasy book that I've read but towards the end, I did really start it enjoy it. </span>

<div id="review_961369170" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/961369170" />
    <a title="Sarah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3344685-sarah"><img alt="Sarah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1388694025p2/3344685.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/961369170?book_show_action=true">Jun 08, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah" href="/user/show/3344685-sarah">Sarah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781447260820" href="/book/show/22087268-trial-by-fire">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3344685-sarah?shelf=books-i-own-kindle">books-i-own-kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3344685-sarah?shelf=read-in-2014">read-in-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3344685-sarah?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3344685-sarah?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3344685-sarah?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3344685-sarah?shelf=books-i-own-print">books-i-own-print</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3344685-sarah?shelf=for-review-read">for-review-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer961369170" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17012388520952840436">Buddy read with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/937889961' rel='nofollow noopener'>Ange</a><br/><br/>I have to confess that I wasn't really too sure what to expect from <b>Trial by Fire</b>, I hadn't heard a great deal about it before I started reading but the shiny foil cover caught my eye and when I realised it was about witches and alternate realities I couldn't resist. I'm so glad I took a chance because this turned out to be one of my favourite YA reads of the year. There is just so much to love about this book and once I'd started reading I didn't want to stop.<br/><br/>Lily is such a </span>
  <span id="freeText17012388520952840436" style="display:none">Buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/937889961" rel="nofollow noopener">Ange</a><br /><br />I have to confess that I wasn't really too sure what to expect from <b>Trial by Fire</b>, I hadn't heard a great deal about it before I started reading but the shiny foil cover caught my eye and when I realised it was about witches and alternate realities I couldn't resist. I'm so glad I took a chance because this turned out to be one of my favourite YA reads of the year. There is just so much to love about this book and once I'd started reading I didn't want to stop.<br /><br />Lily is such a fantastic main character. She isn't one of the popular crowd at school, in fact her allergies to pretty much everything have made her a bit of an outcast but no matter how tough things are she just gets on with it. She knows that it won't be long before her increasing allergies leave her housebound and she's determined to make the most of attending school while she still can. I loved her automatically for having so much courage but what tipped me over the edge into complete girl crush mode was the way she reacted when a potential love interest broke her heart. Lily isn't a simpering fool who will forgive a guy any asshat behaviour just because he is hot, no Lily is the kind of heroine who knows exactly how she deserves to be treated and who would rather be alone than let a boy walk all over her. Do you know how rare a heroine like that is in YA these days? It's so hard to find positive female role models and I could have jumped for job at Lily's response to the boy in question!<br /><br />All that was before we'd made it beyond the first couple of chapters and I could already tell I was going to love this book. Now take this fabulous heroine and drop her unexpectedly into an alternate reality, one where magic is real and where witches rule. Lily suddenly has an explanation for her allergies and finds herself in a place where she isn't an outcast, in fact she is incredibly powerful. She is completely out of her depth and has no idea who she can trust so it's understandable that she quickly bonds with the people she recognises from her own reality but even then she doesn't blindly trust them or expect them to act the way they would in her world. Lily is sensible, she thinks things through and trusts her instincts rather than go along with what other people want her to do, even in an alternate universe Lily is my kind of heroine!<br /><br />There are two other characters who I really want to talk about and the first is Lillian, Lily's alternate self, who happens to be the witch in charge of the whole of Salem and all of the other covens around the new world. Lillian is a fascinating character, she does some horrific things and you can't help but hate her for them but the more you learn about her the more you start to wonder about her motives. I'm not saying her actions are justifiable but she does have reasons and I think we've only started to uncover them. There is so much more to Lillian than a cardboard cut-out villain and the choices she makes raise some really interesting questions. Can you ever justify doing terrible things? Is it worth losing the life of a few people if you can potentially save thousands? What if the cost is more than a few - how much life are you willing to sacrifice?<br /><br />The other character who deserves an honourable mention and a round of applause is love interest Rowan. He really is the kind of guy that we all wish we could meet, he's strong, protective, caring, intelligent and brave but best of all he can admit when he's made a mistake and he can actually apologise for it! Imagine that - a guy who will say sorry! It's a rare and beautiful thing indeed, especially in YA. There is no alpha asshat behaviour here, yes he's wary of Lily in the beginning but considering he thinks she is is mortal enemy Lillian (because they do look identical after all!) that was completely understandable. To be fair, considering the things that Lillian has done to him I actually thought he reacted quite reasonably to Lily's arrival. I absolutely loved seeing their relationship develop over time, there is no insta-love here and the couple spend time getting to know each other and learning to trust. Lily isn't afraid to call Rowan out when he is unreasonable and he is equally willing to push her when she needs it which makes them very well matched.<br /><br />I don't want to say too much about the alternate world that Lily ends up in because I think it is somewhere that you should have fun exploring for yourself by reading the book. What I will say is that I loved the way magic works, the way it is based on scientific principles and has been so cleverly set up that it comes across as completely believable. I don't have much difficulty thinking there is an alternate universe out there somewhere where magic is real! I think it's quite obvious that I loved this book, I could spend hours writing this review trying to give you more reasons to read it but to be honest if I haven't already sold it to you then probably nothing else I could say will either. If you're only going to take one young adult recommendation from me this year then make it <b>Trial by Fire</b>, this book is such a refreshing change, it breaks so many of the current YA trends and is well worth the money it costs.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17012388520952840436" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_882196530" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/882196530" />
    <a title="Rashika (is tired)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8492956-rashika-is-tired"><img alt="Rashika (is tired)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1476647072p2/8492956.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/882196530?book_show_action=true">Mar 15, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rashika (is tired)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rashika (is tired)" href="/user/show/8492956-rashika-is-tired">Rashika (is tired)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8492956-rashika-is-tired?shelf=sci-fic">sci-fic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8492956-rashika-is-tired?shelf=cute-romance">cute-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8492956-rashika-is-tired?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8492956-rashika-is-tired?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8492956-rashika-is-tired?shelf=totally-worth-it">totally-worth-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8492956-rashika-is-tired?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8492956-rashika-is-tired?shelf=good-female-leads">good-female-leads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8492956-rashika-is-tired?shelf=loved">loved</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8492956-rashika-is-tired?shelf=read-2014">read-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8492956-rashika-is-tired?shelf=awesomeness-redefined">awesomeness-redefined</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer882196530" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18266504112129140550"><i>Trial by Fire</i> was exactly as I had hoped it would be but more. That sounds a little contradictory, doesn't it? I suppose the best way to explain it is that I knew I would love this book but I had no idea how much. Angelini never fails to surprise me.<br/><br/>I remember when I first read <i>Starcrossed</i> and now, reading the first book in her new trilogy, I feel the same way as I felt then. I feel that excitement. I feel the thrill. I feel everything. Yet at the same time, it's obvious how much she has grown a</span>
  <span id="freeText18266504112129140550" style="display:none"><i>Trial by Fire</i> was exactly as I had hoped it would be but more. That sounds a little contradictory, doesn't it? I suppose the best way to explain it is that I knew I would love this book but I had no idea how much. Angelini never fails to surprise me.<br /><br />I remember when I first read <i>Starcrossed</i> and now, reading the first book in her new trilogy, I feel the same way as I felt then. I feel that excitement. I feel the thrill. I feel everything. Yet at the same time, it's obvious how much she has grown as a writer. Angelini knows what she is doing. <br /><br />This book does not start off lightly and if you're like me and don't deal well with anticipation, the first chapter and a half is going to be HARD to read through but once you're past those hard bits, it gets a lot better, I promise.<br /><br />Lily is a fantastic character. She is strong and her strength never fails to amaze me. When 'her' Tristan is a jerk to her, she doesn't just curl up into a ball. She's heartbroken but also realizes that what he did to her, the way he treated her, was wrong and she doesn't just let that go away, she tells him that he was a jerk. That's just one showcase of the strength she possesses. She has to adapt to a whole new world yet she does it realistically. Even though she is quick to understand the mechanics of the new world, she continues to hold the ideologies of her own. She isn't just going to change who she is to adapt to this new world, instead she tries to understand these differences and the reasons behind them. That's what makes her such a likeable character. <br /><br />The secondary characters are just as well developed. I want to start off by mentioning the brilliance that is Lillian. I have NO CLUE how Angelini does it. Lillian isn’t your typical villain and I have to say, I find it incredibly hard to hate her. Her actions are inexcusable yet Angelini still develops her character in a way where it’s possible for us as readers to empathize with her. Okay, so I know many won’t be enthusiastic about empathizing with a villain but just trust me. It’s important to the story. Juliet is a wonderful addition although to be honest, throughout the entirety of the book, I found myself missing Lily’s Juliet. That does speak volumes about Angelini’s character development skills, especially if you find yourself missing a character you knew for 1.5 chapters.<br /><br />Let’s not forget Caleb and Tristan though. I think we get to know more about Tristan (the other version who is a lot nicer) more but I kind of connected to Caleb after a certain event. That said, they are both wonderfully developed as well and I cannot wait to see more of them in the sequels.<br /><br />Speaking of, I still haven’t mentioned Rowan, the love interest. I am all about the romance and while I genuinely enjoyed the romance in this book, I also felt really uncomfortable at times. Knowing that Rowan had loved Lillian in the past and was hurt so badly by her made me uncomfortable. It makes me wonder if Rowan actually has genuine feelings for Lily as an individual or if he sees her as a nicer version of Lillian? Those kinds of questions kept on bothering me as I read the book so it made it harder to enjoy their romance, no matter how sweet it was.<br /><br />What takes the cake is the world building and I am not the least bit surprised by that. If you’ve read Angelini’s <i>Starcrossed</i> trilogy, you’ll know what I am talking about. If you have not, you should go get started on that. Moving back to the world building, I have always loved the idea of parallel universes and this book explores the idea in an interesting way. It’s not a brand new idea but at the same time, Angelini manages to make it original. Angelini does an original take on magic but she also creates an interesting power hierarchy. There isn’t much in-depth world building and we learn more about the differences between this world and our own than we do about the history of this new world, but I think we’ll find out a lot more in the sequels.<br /><br />The plot was so well paced although that’s to be expected in this kind of book. The pages flew by and before I knew it, I only had 30 pages left in the book and had to take a quick break so I wouldn’t die of thirst. <br /><br />The way this book ends has me dying to read the sequel and all I can say is that anyone looking for an interesting book featuring magic, you need to check this out. </span>
  <a data-text-id="18266504112129140550" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_743896447" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/743896447" />
    <a title="Varsha" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7217728-varsha"><img alt="Varsha" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1529386265p2/7217728.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/743896447?book_show_action=true">Oct 18, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Varsha" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Varsha" href="/user/show/7217728-varsha">Varsha</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781447260820" href="/book/show/22087268-trial-by-fire">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7217728-varsha?shelf=favorite-authors">favorite-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7217728-varsha?shelf=i-own">i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7217728-varsha?shelf=best-secondary-characters">best-secondary-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7217728-varsha?shelf=gorgeous-covers">gorgeous-covers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7217728-varsha?shelf=2015-favorites">2015-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7217728-varsha?shelf=best-villains-ever">best-villains-ever</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7217728-varsha?shelf=book-husband">book-husband</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7217728-varsha?shelf=memorable-reads">memorable-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7217728-varsha?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7217728-varsha?shelf=kick-ass-heroine">kick-ass-heroine</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer743896447" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9420674614560136825">Actual rating: 4.5 <br/><br/>It's been awhile since I wrote a proper review so this might be unorganized and rusty, just bear with me. :)<br/><br/><br/>Lilly Proctor is allergic to a lot of things and is always sick which makes it nearly impossible for her to live a normal life. So when she gets an opportunity to go to her first and possibly her last high-school party with her best friend and crush Tristan, she take it. But things don't go the way she expected and after a humiliating experience, Lily wishes to disappear</span>
  <span id="freeText9420674614560136825" style="display:none">Actual rating: 4.5 <br><br>It's been awhile since I wrote a proper review so this might be unorganized and rusty, just bear with me. :)<br><br><br>Lilly Proctor is allergic to a lot of things and is always sick which makes it nearly impossible for her to live a normal life. So when she gets an opportunity to go to her first and possibly her last high-school party with her best friend and crush Tristan, she take it. But things don't go the way she expected and after a humiliating experience, Lily wishes to disappear from her current life. And to her surprise she ends up in another world. A parallel world which is run be a different version of herself. A Salem run by witches.<br><br><i>
  <b>"She was still in a Salem... She just wasn't in her Salem anymore."</b>
</i><br><br>One of the things I love about this book is the alternate universe Lily is thrown into. Josephine Angelini excels at world building and this other world is indeed complex. It's a mixture of magic and science, appearing to be both medieval and modern. The working of this world is utterly fascinating! There are witches, crucibles, mechanics and outlanders and I think the picture below explains them all well. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1433347350i/15086620._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Interesting power hierarchy, isn't it? <br><br><i>
  <b>"Magic is a science only people who are born with a particular talent can do. Actual science can be done by anyone. Repeated by anyone." </b>
</i> <br><br>Moving on to the plot, it progressed rather slowly at first but as soon as the point of no return was reached, it had my eyes glued to the pages of the book. It was confusing initially being thrown into a strange world that our protagonist doesn't know about but Angelini paced it well by including alternate POV'S that gave the readers glimpses of the new world and the political drama. <br><br>I liked Lilly's character a lot. She has a lot of strength and she's not the kind of person who let's a jerk walk all over her. When she realizes the way Tristen treated her was wrong, she doesn't just let that go even though he's her best friend. She calls him out on it and i really admire that about her. She's courageous and resourceful and that's another thing I really liked about her. How realistically she adapted to the new world. Those of you who've read this book know what I'm talking about. When she lands in the different Salem, she's frightened and overwhelmed but is quick to understand the mechanics of it and does what is required to survive and get to a safe place. She's also very stubborn and has a great sense of humor. <br><br>The secondary characters were all incredibly fleshed out and I cannot wait to see more of them.<br><br>Lillian by far is the most interesting character in this trilogy for me. She's the other version of Lilly and the one responsible for Lilly's entry into this alternate Salem. She's also the most powerful witch and the leader/ruler of Salem. She isn't your typical villain and honestly, I still can;t see her as the villain and Angelini has built up her character excellently. Sure she's done terrible things but it's not without reason. I need to know more about her. <br><br><i>
  <b>"I remember what I must do, even if it makes me the villain of my own story." </b>
</i><br><br>Lastly Rowan, the love interest, boy do I love him &lt;3 *I feel like I can't help but fall in love with anyone by that name. Rowan Whitethorn and now Rowan Fall * He's intelligent, caring, strong, protective, brave and most importantly admits to his mistakes when he's wrong. He's wary of Lilly in the beginning and that's understandable seeing as how Lillian turned out be. There's no insta love here thankfully and I loved seeing their relationship grow. <br><br>All in all, Trial by Fire is a fantastic book full of magic, adventure and darkness and the cliffhanger has left me with a dozen unanswered questions which I'm dying to unravel in the sequel Firewalker. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9420674614560136825" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1128930615" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1128930615" />
    <a title="Giselle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5789353-giselle"><img alt="Giselle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605042512p2/5789353.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1128930615?book_show_action=true">Dec 10, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Giselle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Giselle" href="/user/show/5789353-giselle">Giselle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781250068194" href="/book/show/23310784-trial-by-fire">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5789353-giselle?shelf=2014">2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5789353-giselle?shelf=from-netgalley">from-netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5789353-giselle?shelf=arc-electronic">arc-electronic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5789353-giselle?shelf=genre-fantasy">genre-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5789353-giselle?shelf=age-young-adult">age-young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5789353-giselle?shelf=genre-supernatural">genre-supernatural</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5789353-giselle?shelf=requested-for-review">requested-for-review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5789353-giselle?shelf=2-star">2-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5789353-giselle?shelf=genre-witches">genre-witches</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5789353-giselle?shelf=genre-paranormal">genre-paranormal</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1128930615" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3830707902689671091">Lily is allergic to a lot of things, weak and constantly sickened by her allergies, her bright spot in life is her best friend Tristan. Taking her to her first house party, he abandons her for some other girl and she ends up having a seizure from a drink filled with alcohol. As the alcohol threatens her weak body, she finds herself transported into another world. Except this world, there's another Lily who is the most powerful witch in the universe. She finds herself allying with another version</span>
  <span id="freeText3830707902689671091" style="display:none">Lily is allergic to a lot of things, weak and constantly sickened by her allergies, her bright spot in life is her best friend Tristan. Taking her to her first house party, he abandons her for some other girl and she ends up having a seizure from a drink filled with alcohol. As the alcohol threatens her weak body, she finds herself transported into another world. Except this world, there's another Lily who is the most powerful witch in the universe. She finds herself allying with another version of Tristan and Rowan, to help them against the monsters that hunt their very land. <br /><br />So there were a lot of bad bits about this book that I have to say. Racist remarks of Native American Indians deemed as "savages" made me feel uncomfortable. If Lily is such a good person, why didn't she question this at all? Every time she transmutes energy into power for her claimed, she always wants to take them over. And it's the same statement over and over again. Then they all turn into Supermen and start to pull apart limbs. I was kind of horrified about that. I found it vaguely interesting that there the ruling classes were divided between the poor and wealthy. And that the poor were people of colour or mixed races. What I also didn't like was that it was one long info dumping session. It just kept going on and on and I was trying to remember everything, but there was a lot to go through.<br /><br />There was a scene where they were teaching her to harness her power by painting runes on her naked body. And I couldn't understand why it was part of her magic? I also can't help but laugh every time she wanted to touch their willstone. Because to me, claiming sounds just like having one-night stands and all these witches were vying for poor Rowan's attention. I couldn't understand the romance at all. I rolled my eyes when there were always stuck together. One sentence described as his "skin whispering to her." I could barely stomach it. And even though there is a slight love triangle, I still want to know about Rowan and the other universe. <br /><br />The wonderful bits? Even though this world is different than ours, it still had its creative elements. My favourite is bio-luminescent trees that glow only at night. The parallel universe, how different their lives are, the magic and even the world that wasn't quite like ours. There is also something about her writing that made me devour the book in two sittings.<br /><br />Love triangle, parallel universes, automatic witchy powers and oh yes the world is going to end. Pick this one up for the lovely universe, but I do have to warn you there are a lot of cheesy romance bits that I couldn't accept.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3830707902689671091" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
